Q: Which is more plausible, X or Y, as the sentence that will come between R and S? The final answer should be a single word "X", "Y", "Both", or "Neither".
R: Jane was a professor teaching piano to students.
S: Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book.
X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.
Y: None of Jane's students had a lesson that day.
A: Let's think step by step.First, we know that Jane is a professor teaching piano to students. This means that she has students who take lessons from her. 

X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons. This is plausible because it fits with the fact that Jane has students who take lessons from her. It also explains why Jane might be spending the morning sipping coffee and reading a book - perhaps she has some free time before her first lesson of the day. 

Y: None of Jane's students had a lesson that day. This is less plausible because it contradicts the fact that Jane is a professor teaching piano to students. If none of her students had a lesson that day, then why would she be spending the morning at home sipping coffee and reading a book? 

Therefore, the answer is X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons. 
Therefore, the answer is X.
